        </div><div class="casAbstract">Two-dimensional (2D) energy materials showed the promising electrochem. characteristics for Li ion storage.  However, the decreased active surfaces and the sluggish charge/mass transport for beyond-Li ion storage that has potential for large-scale energy storage systems, such as Na or K ion storage, caused by the irreversible re-stacking of 2-dimensional materials during electrode processing remain a major challenge.  Here the authors develop a general interlayer engineering strategy to address the above-mentioned challenges by using 2-dimensional ultrathin vanadyl phosphate (VOPO4) nanosheets as a model material for challenging Na ion storage.  Via controlled intercalation of org. mols., such as triethylene glycol and THF, the Na ion transport in VOPO4 nanosheets was significantly improved.  In addn. to advanced characterization including x-ray diffraction, high-resoln. TEM, and X-ray absorption fine structure to characterize the interlayer and the chem. bonding/configuration between the org. intercalants and the VOPO4 host layers, d. functional theory calcns. are also performed to understand the diffusion behavior of Na ions in the pure and TEG intercalated VOPO4 nanosheets.  Because of the expanded interlayer spacing in combination with the decreased energy barriers for Na ion diffusion, intercalated VOPO4 nanosheets show much improved Na ion transport kinetics and greatly enhanced rate capability and cycling stability for Na ion storage.  The results afford deeper understanding of the interlayer-engineering strategy to improve the Na ion storage performance of the VOPO4 nanosheets.  The results may also shed light on possible multivalent-ion based energy storage such as Mg2+ and Al3+.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref15"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref15" class="refNumLink">15</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit15" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201200087"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Su, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Qiao, S.                         cas_cit16R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">16</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">MoS2 Nanoflowers with Expanded Interlayers as High-Performance Anodes for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Hu, Zhe; Wang, Lixiu; Zhang, Kai; Wang, Jianbin; Cheng, Fangyi; Tao, Zhanliang; Chen, Jun</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Angewandte Chemie, International Edition</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2014</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">53</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">47</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">12794-12798</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ACIEF5</span>;

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Wiley-VCH Verlag GmbH &amp; Co. KGaA</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">MoS2 nanoflowers with expanded interlayer spacing of the (002) plane were synthesized and used as high-performance anode in Na-ion batteries.  By controlling the cut-off voltage to the range of 0.4-3 V, an intercalation mechanism rather than a conversion reaction is taking place.  The MoS2 nanoflower electrode shows high discharge capacities of 350 mAh g-1 at 0.05 A g-1, 300 mAh g-1 at 1 A g-1, and 195 mAh g-1 at 10 A g-1.  An initial capacity increase with cycling is caused by peeling off MoS2 layers, which produces more active sites for Na+ storage.  The stripping of MoS2 layers occurring in charge/discharge cycling contributes to the enhanced kinetics and low energy barrier for the intercalation of Na+ ions.  The electrochem. reaction is mainly controlled by the capacitive process, which facilitates the high-rate capability.  Therefore, MoS2 nanoflowers with expanded interlayers hold promise for rechargeable Na-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref17"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref17" class="refNumLink">17</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit17" data-doi="10.1039/C6TA09831B"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shi, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhao, T.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Recent Advances in Inorganic 2D Materials and Their Applications in Lithium and Sodium Batteries</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Two-dimensional inorg. materials, such as exfoliated graphene, have been under much research attention as of late, for their high surface-to-mass ratio and unique phys. and chem. properties.  Many of these properties are highly sought after in Li/Na-based batteries.  The authors review recent advances in inorg. 2-dimensional materials and summarize their applications as: (i) the electrode materials or additives for Li/Na-ion batteries; (ii) the scaffold or interfacial layer for Li-metal anodes; (iii) the cathode for Li/Na-O2 batteries; and (iv) the anchoring material for Li polysulfides for Li-S batteries.                         cas_cit19R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">19</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A new layered titanate Na2Li2Ti5O12 as a high-performance intercalation anode for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Huang, Yangyang; Wang, Jinsong; Miao, Lin; Jin, Yu; Peng, Jian; Li, Qing; Fang, Chun; Han, Jiantao; Huang, Yunhui</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Currently, it is a great challenge to find suitable electrode materials for Na-ion batteries (SIBs) with large capacity, long cycle life, and high rate capability.  Herein, the authors report a new layered titanate, Na2Li2Ti5O12 (NLT), derived from K2Li2Ti5O12 (KLT) via an ion-exchange method as a SIB anode material.  KLT is prepd. by a low-temp. solid-state reaction and then transformed into NLT by replacing K with Na in a NaCl soln. at room temp.  NLT provides a Na-ion intercalation voltage at ∼0.5 V vs. Na/Na+ and a reversible capacity of 175 mA h g-1 at a c.d. of 100 mA g-1.  It also shows a high Na-ion diffusion coeff. of 3.0 × 10-10 cm2 s-1, ensuring a high rate capability.  For NLT, extremely high discharging rate capability is achieved with a capacity of &gt;80 mA h g-1 at a 60 s full discharge and even with 70 mA h g-1 at a 34 s charge.  Kinetics anal. based on cyclic voltammogram reveals a typical Na-ion intercalation behavior in NLT.  Also, the 1st-principle calcn. shows a lower migration energy barrier for Na ions in NLT than that in other layered titanates.  Probably NLT is a very promising anode material for high-performance SIBs, esp. for fast-charging stable SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref20"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref20" class="refNumLink">20</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit20" data-doi="10.1039/c2ta01057g"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Rudola, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Saravanan, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Mason, C.                         cas_cit20R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">20</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Na2Ti3O7: an intercalation based anode for sodium-ion battery applications</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Rudola, Ashish; Saravanan, Kuppan; Mason, Chad W.; Balaya, Palani</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors report here the electrochem. properties of Na2Ti3O7, a potential non-carbon, low-voltage anode material for room temp. Na-ion battery applications.  A solid-state route was used to prep. Na2Ti3O7.  Further, XRD, SEM, TEM, HR-TEM, SAED, XPS and EDX techniques were used to characterize the material.  The Na/Na2Ti3O7 cell displayed a charge capacity of 177 mA h g-1 at 0.1 C rate.  High rate and long term cyclic performance at different rates showed relatively stable storage capacities.  Surprisingly, if the lower cut-off voltage is altered, the appearance of a new charge plateau is seen, with no apparent change in the discharge behavior.         </div><div class="casAbstract">In this work, we investigated several titanates with lepidocrocite-type structures (general formula AxTi1-yMyO4, with A = Na and M = Li or Mg), having potential utility as anode materials for sodium-ion batteries. Site limitations were found to be crit. determinants of the gravimetric capacities, which are also affected both by the stacking arrangement of the corrugated layers and the identity of M (Li or Mg). Sodium diffusion barriers were also found to vary as a function of state of charge and diffusion direction, with a spread of 0.06-1.3 eV at low sodium contents, narrowing to 0.3-0.5 eV at higher sodium contents. Nowadays, electrochem. energy storage technologies and applications have attracted much attention, including portable elec. devices, elec. vehicles and smart power grids.  Lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) have been widely applied in these areas because of their safety, portability and high energy d.         </div><div class="casAbstract">For reasons of cost and supply security issues, there is growing interest in the development of rechargeable sodium ion batteries, particularly for large-scale grid storage applications.  Like the much better known and technol. important lithium ion analogs, the devices operate by shuttling alkali metal cations between two host materials, which undergo insertion processes at different electrochem. potentials.  A particular challenge for the sodium systems is identification of a suitable anode material due to the fact that sodium does not intercalate into graphite.  Although several alternatives, including disordered carbons and alloys are being investigated, the most promising options at present lie with titanates, not in the least because of attractive characteristics such as low toxicity, ease of synthesis, wide availability, and low cost.  A large variety of sodium titanate compds. can be prepd., many of which have tunnel or layered structures that can readily undergo reversible reductive intercalation reactions.  A brief overview of the phys., structural, and electrochem. characteristics of several of the most promising materials for sodium-ion battery applications is given in this paper, and a comparison is made between the sodium and the lithium insertion behaviors.  For some of these compds., insertion of sodium occurs at unusually low potentials, a feature that has important implications for the design of high-energy sodium-ion systems.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref25" class="refNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit25" data-doi="10.1039/C6EE01807F"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yi, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Recent Advances in Titanium-Based Electrode Materials for Stationary Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Energy Environ.                         cas_cit26R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">26</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Lepidocrocite-type layered titanate structures: new lithium and sodium ion intercalation anode materials</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Shirpour, Mona; Cabana, Jordi; Doeff, Marca</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Chemistry of Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">The electrochem. characteristics of lepidocrocite-type titanates derived from K0.8Ti1.73Li0.27O4 are presented for the first time.  By exchanging sodium ions for potassium, the practical specific capacity of the titanate in both sodium and lithium half cells is considerably enhanced.  Although the gross structural features of the titanate framework are maintained during the ion exchange process, the symmetry changes because sodium occupies different sites from potassium.  The smaller size of the sodium ion as compared to potassium and the change in site symmetry allow more alkali metal cations to be inserted reversibly into the structure during discharge in sodium and lithium cells than in the parent compd.  Insertion of lithium cations takes place at an av. of about 0.8 V vs Li+/Li while sodium intercalation occurs at 0.5 V vs Na+/Na, with sloping voltage profiles exhibited for both cell configurations, implying single-phase processes.  Ex situ synchrotron X-ray diffraction measurements show that a lithiated lepidocrocite is formed during discharge in lithium cells, which undergoes further lithium insertion with almost no vol. change.  In sodium cells, insertion of sodium initially causes an overall expansion of about 12% in the b lattice parameter, but reversible uptake of solvent minimizes changes upon further cycling.  In the case of the sodium cells, both the practical capacity and the cyclability are improved when a more compliant binder (polyacrylic acid) that can accommodate vol. changes assocd. with insertion processes is used in place of the more common polyvinylidene fluoride.  The ability to tune the electrochem. properties of lepidocrocite titanate structures by varying compns. and utilizing ion exchange processes make them esp. versatile anode materials for both lithium and sodium ion battery configurations.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref27" class="refNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit27" data-doi="10.1021/acsaem.8b00170"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Reeves, K.                         cas_cit27R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">27</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Insights into Li+, Na+, and K+ Intercalation in Lepidocrocite-Type Layered TiO2 Structures</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Reeves, Kyle G.; Ma, Jiwei; Fukunishi, Mika; Salanne, Mathieu; Komaba, Shinichi; Dambournet, Damien</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Energy Materials</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A lamellar lepidocrocite-type titanate structure with ∼25% Ti4+ vacancies was recently synthesized, and it showed potential for use as an electrode in rechargeable lithium-ion batteries.  In addn. to Li, we explore this material's ability to accommodate other monovalent ions with greater natural abundance (e.g., Na and K) in order to develop lower-cost alternatives to Li-ion batteries constructed from more widely available elements.  Galvanostatic discharge/charge curves for the lepidocrocite material indicate that increasing the ionic radius of the monovalent ion results in a deteriorating performance of the electrode.  Using 1st-principles electronic structure calcns., we identify the relaxed geometries of the structure for various placement of the ion in the structure.  We then use these geometries to compute the energy of formations.  We det. that all ions are favorable in the structure, but interlayer positions are preferred compared to vacancy positions.  We also conclude that the exchange between the interlayer and vacancy positions is a process which involves the interaction between interlayer water and surface hydroxyl groups next to the titanate layer.  We observe a cooperative effect between structural water and OH groups to assist alkali-ions to move from the interlayer to the vacancy site.         </div><div class="casAbstract">First principle DFT calcns. are used to study the thermodn. and kinetic properties of Na-ion insertion in TiO2 hollandite, a potential anode for Na-ion batteries.  The exptl. obsd. phase transformation from tetragonal TiO2 (I4/m) to monoclinic Na0.25TiO2 (I2/m) is confirmed.  At high Na-ion concns. the calcd. formation energies predict a first-order phase transition toward the layered O'3-Na0.68TiO2 structure.  Further sodiation initiates a solid soln. reaction toward the layered O3-NaTiO2 phase, which was recently brought forward as a promising anode for Na-ion batteries.  This transformation irreversibly transforms the one-dimensional hollandite tunnel structure into the layered structure and potentially brings forward an alternative route toward the prepn. of the hard to prep. O3-NaTiO2 material.  Energy barrier calcns. reveal fast Na-ion diffusion at low concns. and sluggish diffusion upon reaching the N0.25TiO2 phase, rationalizing why exptl. the Na0.5TiO2 phase is not achieved.  Detailed anal. of the kinetic behavior in the hollandite structure via mol. dynamics simulations reveals the importance of correlated at. motions and dynamic lattice deformations for the Na-ion diffusion.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Insertion type material has been attracted plenty of attentions as the anode of sodium ion batteries (SIBs) due to the low vol. change induced long cycle stability.  H1.07Ti1.73O4 (HTO), a two-dimensional layered material, is a new insertion type anode material for SIBs reported in this study. This exfoliation process is considered to be time-consuming, hindering their industrial-scale prodn.  Based on in situ exfoliation studies on the protonated layered titanate H1.07Ti1.73O4·H2O (HTO), it is now shown that ion intercalation-assisted exfoliation driven by chem. reaction provides a viable and fast route to isolated nanosheets. However, the layered materials suffer low thermal stability after the soln. processes.  Herein, we report a strategy to improve the thermal stability of the layered materials processed in soln.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The authors present an efficient scheme for calcg. the Kohn-Sham ground state of metallic systems using pseudopotentials and a plane-wave basis set.  In the first part the application of Pulay's DIIS method (direct inversion in the iterative subspace) to the iterative diagonalization of large matrixes will be discussed.  This approach is stable, reliable, and minimizes the no. of order Natoms3 operations.  In the second part, we will discuss an efficient mixing scheme also based on Pulay's scheme.  A special "metric" and a special "preconditioning" optimized for a plane-wave basis set will be introduced.  Scaling of the method will be discussed in detail for non-self-consistent and self-consistent calcns.  It will be shown that the no. of iterations required to obtain a specific precision is almost independent of the system size.  Altogether an order Natoms2 scaling is found for systems contg. up to 1000 electrons.  If we take into account that the no. of k points can be decreased linearly with the system size, the overall scaling can approach Natoms.  They have implemented these algorithms within a powerful package called VASP (Vienna ab initio simulation package).  The program and the techniques have been used successfully for a large no. of different systems (liq. and amorphous semiconductors, liq. simple and transition metals, metallic and semiconducting surfaces, phonons in simple metals, transition metals, and semiconductors) and turned out to be very reliable.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref34"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref34" class="refNumLink">34</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit34" data-doi="10.1063/1.472933"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Perdew, J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">D. functional approxns. for the exchange-correlation energy ExcDFA of an electronic system are often improved by admixing some exact exchange Ex: Exc ≈ ExcDFA + (1/n)(Ex - ExDFA).  This procedure is justified when the error in ExcDFA arises from the λ = 0 or exchange end of the coupling-const. integral ∫01dλ Exc,λDFA.  We argue that the optimum integer n is approx. the lowest order of Goerling-Levy perturbation theory which provides a realistic description of the coupling-const. dependence Exc,λ in the range 0 ≤ λ ≤ 1, whence n ≈ 4 for atomization energies of typical mols.  We also propose a continuous generalization of n as an index of correlation strength, and a possible mixing of second-order perturbation theory with the generalized gradient approxn.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref35"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref35" class="refNumLink">35</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit35" data-doi="10.1063/1.3382344"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Grimme, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Antony, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ehrlich, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Krieg, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">A Consistent and Accurate Ab Initio Parametrization of Density Functional Dispersion Correction (DFT-D) for the 94 Elements H-Pu</span>. <i>J.                         cas_cit35R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">35</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">A consistent and accurate ab initio parametrization of density functional dispersion correction (DFT-D) for the 94 elements H-Pu</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Grimme, Stefan; Antony, Jens; Ehrlich, Stephan; Krieg, Helge</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Chemical Physics</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2010</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">132</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">15</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">154104/1-154104/19</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JCPSA6</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">0021-9606</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Institute of Physics</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The method of dispersion correction as an add-on to std. Kohn-Sham d. functional theory (DFT-D) has been refined regarding higher accuracy, broader range of applicability, and less empiricism.  The main new ingredients are atom-pairwise specific dispersion coeffs. and cutoff radii that are both computed from first principles.  The coeffs. for new eighth-order dispersion terms are computed using established recursion relations.  System (geometry) dependent information is used for the first time in a DFT-D type approach by employing the new concept of fractional coordination nos. (CN).  They are used to interpolate between dispersion coeffs. of atoms in different chem. environments.  The method only requires adjustment of two global parameters for each d. functional, is asymptotically exact for a gas of weakly interacting neutral atoms, and easily allows the computation of at. forces.  Three-body nonadditivity terms are considered.  The method has been assessed on std. benchmark sets for inter- and intramol. noncovalent interactions with a particular emphasis on a consistent description of light and heavy element systems.  The mean abs. deviations for the S22 benchmark set of noncovalent interactions for 11 std. d. functionals decrease by 15%-40% compared to the previous (already accurate) DFT-D version.  Spectacular improvements are found for a tripeptide-folding model and all tested metallic systems.  The rectification of the long-range behavior and the use of more accurate C6 coeffs. also lead to a much better description of large (infinite) systems as shown for graphene sheets and the adsorption of benzene on an Ag(111) surface.  For graphene it is found that the inclusion of three-body terms substantially (by about 10%) weakens the interlayer binding.  We propose the revised DFT-D method as a general tool for the computation of the dispersion energy in mols. and solids of any kind with DFT and related (low-cost) electronic structure methods for large systems.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Photocatalysts show great potential in environmental remediation and water splitting using either artificial or natural light.  Titanium dioxide (TiO2)-based photocatalysts are studied most frequently because they are stable, non-toxic, readily available, and highly efficient.  However, the relatively wide band gap of TiO2 significantly limits its use under visible light or solar light.  We herein report a facile route for controllable synthesis of Ti3+-doped TiO2 with tunable photocatalytic properties using a hydrothermal method with varying amts. of reductant, i.e., sodium borohydride (NaBH4).  The resulting TiO2 showed color changes from light yellow, light gray, to dark gray with the increasing amountof NaBH4.  The present method can controllably and effectively reduce Ti4+ on the surface of TiO2 and induce partial transformation of anatase TiO2 to rutile TiO2, with the evolution of nanoparticles into hierarchical structures attributable to a high pressure and strong alkali environment in the synthesis atm.; in this way, the photocatalytic activity of Ti3+-doped TiO2 under visible-light can be tuned.  The as-developed strategy may open up a new avenue for designing and functionalizing TiO2 materials for enhancing visible light absorption, narrowing band gap, and improving photocatalytic activity.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref40"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref40" class="refNumLink">40</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit40" data-doi="10.1021/cm901329g"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gao, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Fjellvåg, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Norby, P.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Defect Chemistry of a Zinc-Doped Lepidocrocite Titanate Cs<sub>x</sub>Ti<sub>2–x/2</sub>Zn<sub>x/2</sub>O<sub>4</sub> (x = 0.7) and its Protonic Form</span>. <i>Chem.                         cas_cit44R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">44</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Nanostructured Na2Ti9O19 for Hybrid Sodium-Ion Capacitors with Excellent Rate Capability</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Bhat, Swetha S. M.; Babu, Binson; Feygenson, Mikhail; Neuefeind, Joerg C.; Shaijumon, M. M.</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2018</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">10</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">1</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">437-447</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">AAMICK</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1944-8244</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Herein, we report a new Na-insertion electrode material, Na2Ti9O19, as a potential candidate for Na-ion hybrid capacitors.  We study the structural properties of nanostructured Na2Ti9O19, synthesized by a hydrothermal technique, upon electrochem. cycling vs Na.  Av. and local structures of Na2Ti9O19 are elucidated from neutron Rietveld refinement and pair distribution function (PDF), resp., to investigate the initial discharge and charge events.  Rietveld refinement reveals electrochem. cycling of Na2Ti9O19 is driven by single-phase solid soln. reaction during (de)sodiation without any major structural deterioration, keeping the av. structure intact.  Unit cell vol. and lattice evolution on discharge process is inherently related to TiO6 distortion and Na ion perturbations, while the PDF reveals the deviation in the local structure after sodiation.  Raman spectroscopy and XPS studies further corroborate the av. and local structural behavior derived from neutron diffraction measurements.  Also, Na2Ti9O19 shows excellent Na-ion kinetics with a capacitve nature of 86% at 1.0 mV s-1, indicating that the material is a good anode candidate for a sodium-ion hybrid capacitor.  A full cell hybrid Na-ion capacitor is fabricated by using Na2Ti9O19 as anode and activated porous carbon as cathode, which exhibits excellent electrochem. properties, with a max. energy d. of 54 Wh kg-1 and a max. power d. of 5 kW kg-1.                         cas_cit51R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">51</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In Situ Formation of Conductive Metal Sulfide Domain in Metal Oxide Matrix: An Efficient Way to Improve the Electrochemical Activity of Semiconducting Metal Oxide</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Kim, In Young; Seo, Jiyoon; Oh, Seung Mi; Patil, Sharad B.; Hwang, Seong-Ju</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Advanced Functional Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">A new effective way to improve the electrochem. activity of semiconducting metal oxide is developed by the in situ formation of conductive metal sulfide domain in the metal oxide matrix.  The Li0.96Ti1.08S2-Li4Ti5O12 nanocomposites with tunable compns. and elec. properties are synthesized by the reaction of Li4Ti5O12 with CS2 at elevated temp. As anode materials for Li ion batteries, the obtained Li0.96Ti1.08S2-Li4Ti5O12 nanocomposites show much greater discharge capacity and better rate characteristics than does the pristine Li4Ti5O12.  The usefulness of the present method is further evidenced from the improvement of the electrochem. activity of semiconducting CsTi2NbO7 after the reaction with CS2.  The present study clearly demonstrates the in situ formation of conductive metal sulfide domain using CS2 liq. can provide an efficient and universal way to improve the electrode functionality of semiconducting metal oxide.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref52"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref52" class="refNumLink">52</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit52" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.6b00208"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Adpakpang, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jin, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Oh, S.                         cas_cit52R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">52</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Unusually Huge Charge Storage Capacity of Mn3O4-Graphene Nanocomposite Achieved by Incorporation of Inorganic Nanosheets</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Adpakpang, Kanyaporn; Jin, Xiaoyan; Lee, Seul; Oh, Seung Mi; Lee, Nam-Suk; Hwang, Seong-Ju</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Remarkable improvement in electrode performance of Mn3O4-graphene nanocomposites for lithium ion batteries can be obtained by incorporation of a small amt. of exfoliated layered MnO2 or RuO2 nanosheets.  The metal oxide nanosheet-incorporated Mn3O4-reduced graphene oxide (rGO) nanocomposites are synthesized via growth of Mn3O4 nanocrystals in the mesoporous networks of rGO and MnO2/RuO2 2D nanosheets.  Incorporation of metal oxide nanosheets is highly effective in optimizing porous composite structure and charge transport properties, resulting in a remarkable increase of discharge capacity of Mn3O4-rGO nanocomposite with significant improvement of cyclability and rate performance.  The obsd. enormous discharge capacity of synthesized Mn3O4-rGO-MnO2 nanocomposite (∼1600 mA·h·g-1 for the 100th cycle) is the highest value among reported data for Mn3O4-rGO nanocomposite.  Despite much lower elec. cond. of MnO2 than RuO2, the MnO2-incorporated nanocomposite at optimal compn. (2.5 wt %) shows even larger discharge capacities with comparable rate characteristics compared with the RuO2-incorporated homolog.  This finding underscores that the electrode performance of the resulting nanosheet-incorporated nanocomposite is strongly dependent on its pore and composite structures rather than on the intrinsic elec. cond. of the additive nanosheet.  The present study clearly demonstrates that, regardless of elec. cond., incorporation of metal oxide 2D nanosheet is an effective way to efficiently optimize the electrode functionality of graphene-based nanocomposites.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref53"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref53" class="refNumLink">53</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit53" data-doi="10.1016/j.jpowsour.2022.230994"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Nie, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cheng, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Q.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tian, F.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yao, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Liang, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lu, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Surface Organic Nitrogen-Doping Disordered Biomass Carbon Materials with Superior Cycle Stability in the Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J.         </div><div class="casAbstract">To achieve widespread application of sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) in the future new energy market, developing electrode materials with low-cost sustainability and excellent electrochem. properties is imperative.  Herein, a mesoporous N-doping palm leaf-based hard carbon (PLHC-N) anode with a high-rate and long lifespan is synthesized via an in-situ polymn. method by using palm leaf as the carbon precursor and polyaniline as the nitrogen source.  Benefiting from the natural holey structure, the PLHC-N exhibits excellent Na+ storage capability with numerous ion transfer channels and a good vol. buffer.  Meanwhile, the N-doping materials improve ion and electron transferability and create more active sites for Na storage.  Impressively, the PLHC-N sample shows an adsorption-intercalation-hole filling storage mechanism and affords an ultrahigh reversible capacity of 373 mAh g-1 at 25 mA g-1, and long-term cycle stability at 200 mA g-1 (∼95.0% retention upon 1000 cycles).  Moreover, a full cell with a Na3V2(PO4)2F3 as cathode shows a favorable cyclability (112 mA h g-1 after 100 cycles at 0.5C (1C = 128 mA g-1) and a decent capacity retention of 90.1%).  Given the cost effectiveness and material sustainability, our work provides novel strategy to design the hard carbon anode materials for advanced SIBs.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref54"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref54" class="refNumLink">54</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit54" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.5b06958"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kajiyama, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Szabova, L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sodeyama, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Iinuma, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Morita, R.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Gotoh, K.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Tateyama, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Okubo, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yamada, A.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Sodium-Ion Intercalation Mechanism in MXene Nanosheets</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2016</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>10</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">3334</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">3341</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:

        </div><div class="casAbstract">Herein, using solid-state 23Na magic angle spinning NMR and d. functional theory calcn., the authors reveal that MXene Ti3C2Tx in a nonaq. Na+ electrolyte exhibits reversible Na+ intercalation/deintercalation into the interlayer space.  Detailed analyses demonstrate that Ti3C2Tx undergoes expansion of the interlayer distance during the first sodiation, whereby desolvated Na+ is intercalated/deintercalated reversibly.  The interlayer distance is maintained during the whole sodiation/desodiation process due to the pillaring effect of trapped Na+ and the swelling effect of penetrated solvent mols. between the Ti3C2Tx sheets. Here we demonstrate a high-capacity and high-rate sodium-ion anode based on ultrathin layered tin(II) sulfide nanostructures, in which a maximized extrinsic pseudocapacitance contribution is identified and verified by kinetics anal.                         cas_cit56R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">56</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">In situ nitrogen doping of TiO2 by plasma enhanced atomic layer deposition for enhanced sodium storage performance</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Lin, Jinhuan; Ma, Dingtao; Li, Yongliang; Zhang, Peixin; Mi, Hongwei; Deng, Libo; Sun, Lingna; Ren, Xiangzhong</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Dalton Transactions</span>

    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">46</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">38</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">13101-13107</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">DTARAF</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1477-9226</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Nitrogen-doped TiO2 is in situ synthesized by plasma enhanced at. layer deposition on carbon nanotubes (N-TiO2/CNTs).  The prepd. N-TiO2/CNT nanocomposites are employed as anode materials for sodium ion batteries.  The specific capacity of an N-TiO2/CNT electrode is 1.45 times higher than that of a TiO2/CNT electrode at a c.d. of 50 mA g-1 after 200 cycles.  It is demonstrated that N-TiO2/CNTs are more effective in an electrochem. Na cell due to the enhanced kinetics which results from the nitrogen-doping and the amorphous feature.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref57"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref57" class="refNumLink">57</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit57" data-doi="10.1039/C6TA10494K"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yun, B.-N.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Du, H. L.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Hwang, J.-Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Jung, H.-G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.-K.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Improved Electrochemical Performance of Boron-Doped Carbon-Coated Lithium Titanate as an Anode Material for Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>J. Mater. Chem. A</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2017</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>5</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">2802</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">2810</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1039/C6TA10494K</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D5%26publication_year%3D2017%26pages%3D2802-2810%26journal%3DJ.%2BMater.%2BChem.%2BA%26author%3DB.-N.%2BYun%26author%3DH.%2BL.%2BDu%26author%3DJ.-Y.%2BHwang%26author%3DH.-G.%2BJung%26author%3DY.-K.%2BSun%26title%3DImproved%2BElectrochemical%2BPerformance%2Bof%2BBoron-Doped%2BCarbon-Coated%2BLithium%2BTitanate%2Bas%2Ban%2BAnode%2BMaterial%2Bfor%2BSodium-Ion%2BBatteries%26doi%3D10.1039%252FC6TA10494K&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.2c15359&amp;doiOfLink=10.1039%2FC6TA10494K&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit57R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">57</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Improved electrochemical performance of boron-doped carbon-coated lithium titanate as an anode material for sodium-ion batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Yun, Bin-Na; Du, Hoang Long; Hwang, Jang-Yeon; Jung, Hun-Gi; Sun, Yang-Kook</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Materials Chemistry A: Materials for Energy and Sustainability</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2017</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">5</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">2802-2810</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">JMCAET</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2050-7496</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">A B-doped C layer (BC) was coated on porous micron-sized Li4Ti5O12 (LTO) via a facile wet-chem. method for use as a promising anode material for Na-ion batteries.  As detd. by x-ray photoemission spectroscopy and Raman spectroscopy, 3 different species (BC3, BC2O, and BCO2) were doped in the C layer on the surface of LTO.  These heteroatoms lead to abundant extrinsic defects in the C layer that result in improved Na-ion diffusivity across the active material.  Using electrochem. impedance spectroscopy, the diffusion coeff. of the B-doped C-coated LTO (BC-LTO) is 2.241 × 10-15 cm2 s-1.  The BC-LTO exhibited 85% and 60% higher Na-ion diffusivity than pristine LTO and C-coated LTO (C-LTO), resp.  Also, electron-deficient B in BC3 enhances the elec. cond. through pos. charged holes that carry electrons through the C structure.  Accordingly, the BC-LTO electrode showed a high specific capacity of 148 mA-h g-1 at 0.5 C and 98.4 mA-h g-1 at 10C rate.  The BC-LTO anode demonstrated a great capacity retention of ∼90% at 1 and 10C after 300 cycles.  These findings demonstrate the promising potential of LTO as a high-performance anode material for Na-ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="ref58"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="javascript:void(0);" data-citation="" data-rid="ref58" class="refNumLink">58</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="cit58" data-doi="10.1021/acsnano.2c01186"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Huang, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, W.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, B.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Xu, T.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zang, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kong, D.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Li, X.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yang, H. Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wang, Y.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">3D-Printed Sodiophilic V<sub>2</sub>CT<sub>x</sub>/rGO-CNT MXene Microgrid Aerogel for Stable Na Metal Anode with High Areal Capacity</span>. <i>ACS Nano</i>  <span class="NLM_year" style="font-weight: bold;">2022</span>,  <span class="NLM_volume"><i>16</i></span>,  <span class="NLM_fpage">9105</span>– <span class="NLM_lpage">9116</span>, <span class="refDoi">&nbsp;DOI:
                10.1021/acsnano.2c01186</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><span class="references__suffix"><a class="google-scholar" href="/action/getFTRLinkout?url=http%3A%2F%2Fscholar.google.com%2Fscholar_lookup%3Fhl%3Den%26volume%3D16%26publication_year%3D2022%26pages%3D9105-9116%26journal%3DACS%2BNano%26author%3DZ.%2BWang%26author%3DZ.%2BHuang%26author%3DH.%2BWang%26author%3DW.%2BLi%26author%3DB.%2BWang%26author%3DJ.%2BXu%26author%3DT.%2BXu%26author%3DJ.%2BZang%26author%3DD.%2BKong%26author%3DX.%2BLi%26author%3DH.%2BY.%2BYang%26author%3DY.%2BWang%26title%3D3D-Printed%2BSodiophilic%2BV2CTx%252FrGO-CNT%2BMXene%2BMicrogrid%2BAerogel%2Bfor%2BStable%2BNa%2BMetal%2BAnode%2Bwith%2BHigh%2BAreal%2BCapacity%26doi%3D10.1021%252Facsnano.2c01186&amp;doi=10.1021%2Facsami.2c15359&amp;doiOfLink=10.1021%2Facsnano.2c01186&amp;linkType=gs&amp;linkLocation=Reference&amp;linkSource=FULL_TEXT" target="_blank">Google Scholar</a></span><div class="casRecord" id="
                        cas_cit58R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">58</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">3D-Printed Sodiophilic V2CTx/rGO-CNT MXene Microgrid Aerogel for Stable Na Metal Anode with High Areal Capacity</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Wang, Zixuan; Huang, Zhenxin; Wang, Hui; Li, Weidong; Wang, Bingyan; Xu, Junmin; Xu, Tingting; Zang, Jinhao; Kong, Dezhi; Li, Xinjian; Yang, Hui Ying; Wang, Ye</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Nano</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2022</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">16</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">6</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:pages">9105-9116</span>CODEN:
                <span class="NLM_cas:coden">ANCAC3</span>;
        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">1936-0851</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">Featuring a high theor. capacity, low cost, and abundant resources, sodium metal has emerged as an ideal anode material for sodium ion batteries.  However, the real feasibility of sodium metal anodes is still hampered by the uncontrolled sodium dendrite problems.  Herein, an artificial three-dimensional (3D) hierarchical porous sodiophilic V2CTx/rGO-CNT microgrid aerogel is fabricated by a direct-ink writing 3D printing technol. and further adopted as the matrix of Na metal to deliver a Na@V2CTx/rGO-CNT sodium metal anode.  Upon cycling, the V2CTx/rGO-CNT electrode can yield a superior cycling life of more than 3000 h (2 mA cm-2, 10 mAh cm-2) with an av. Coulombic efficiency of 99.54%.  More attractively, it can even sustain a stable operation over 900 h at 5 mA cm-2 with an ultrahigh areal capacity of 50 mAh cm-2.  In situ and exsitu characterizations and d. functional theory simulation analyses prove that V2CTx with abundant sodiophilic functional groups can effectively guide the sodium metal nucleation and uniform deposition, thus enabling a dendrite-free morphol.  Moreover, a full cell pairing a Na@V2CTx/rGO-CNT anode with a Na3V2(PO4)3@C-rGO cathode can deliver a high reversible capacity of 86.27 mAh g-1 after 400 cycles at 100 mA g-1.  This work not only clarifies the superior Na deposition chem. on the sodiophilic V2CTx/rGO-CNT microgrid aerogel electrode but also offers an approach for fabricating advanced Na metal anodes via a 3D printing method.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li></ol></div><script type="text/javascript"         </div><div class="casAbstract">A review.  Energy prodn. and storage have become key issues concerning our welfare in daily life.  Present challenges for batteries are twofold.  In the first place, the increasing demand for powering systems of portable electronic devices and zero-emission vehicles stimulates research towards high energy and high voltage systems.  In the second place, low cost batteries are required in order to advance towards smart elec. grids that integrate discontinuous energy flow from renewable sources, optimizing the performance of clean energy sources.  Na-ion batteries can be the key for the second point, because of the huge availability of sodium, its low price and the similarity of both Li and Na insertion chemistries.  In spite of the lower energy d. and voltage of Na-ion based technologies, they can be focused on applications where the wt. and footprint requirement is less drastic, such as elec. grid storage.  Much work has to be done in the field of Na-ion in order to catch up with Li-ion technol.  Cathodic and anodic materials must be optimized, and new electrolytes will be the key point for Na-ion success.  This review will gather the up-to-date knowledge about Na-ion battery materials, with the aim of providing a wide view of the systems that have already been explored and a starting point for the new research on this battery technol.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref2"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref2" class="rightTabRefNumLink">2</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit2" data-doi="10.1002/aenm.201600943"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kim, H.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Ding, Z.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Lee, M.     <span class="NLM_cas:volume">13</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue">3</span>),

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Royal Society of Chemistry</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The conventional P2-type cathode material Na0.67Ni0.33Mn0.67O2 suffers from an irreversible P2-O2 phase transition and serious capacity fading during cycling.  Here, we successfully carry out magnesium and calcium ion doping into the transition-metal layers (TM layers) and the alkali-metal layers (AM layers), resp., of Na0.67Ni0.33Mn0.67O2.  Both Mg and Ca doping can reduce O-type stacking in the high-voltage region, leading to enhanced cycling endurance, however, this is assocd. with a decrease in capacity.  The results of d. functional theory (DFT) studies reveal that the introduction of Mg2+ and Ca2+ make high-voltage reactions (oxygen redox and Ni4+/Ni3+ redox reactions) less accessible.  Thanks to the synergetic effect of co-doping with Mg2+ and Ca2+ ions, the adverse effects on high-voltage reactions involving Ni-O bonding are limited, and the structural stability is further enhanced.  The finally obtained P2-type Na0.62Ca0.025Ni0.28Mg0.05Mn0.67O2 exhibits a satisfactory initial energy d. of 468.2 W h kg-1 and good capacity retention of 83% after 100 cycles at 50 mA g-1 within the voltage range of 2.2-4.35 V.  This work deepens our understanding of the specific effects of Mg2+ and Ca2+ dopants and provides a stability-enhancing strategy utilizing abundant alk. earth elements.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref5"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref5" class="rightTabRefNumLink">5</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit5" data-doi="10.1021/acsami.8b07031"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Piao, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Oh, S.                         rightTab-cas_cit5R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">5</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Critical Role of the Chemical Environment of Interlayer Na Sites: An Effective Way To Improve the Na Ion Electrode Activity of Layered Titanate</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Piao, Meina; Oh, Seung Mi; Lim, Joohyun; Kim, Sun Ha; Kim, Sung-Chul; Jo, Yun Kyung; Han, Oc Hee; Hwang, Seong-Ju</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">ACS Applied Materials &amp; Interfaces</span>

            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">American Chemical Society</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The chem. environments of the interlayer Na sites of layered titanate are finely controlled by the intercalation of n-alkylamine with various alkyl chain lengths to explore an effective way to improve its electrode functionality for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs).  The n-alkylamine intercalation via ion-exchange and exfoliation-restacking routes allows the modification of in-plane structures of layered titanate to be tuned.  Among the present n-alkylamine-intercalates, the n-pentylamine-intercalated titanate shows the largest discharge capacity with the best rate characteristics, underscoring the crit. role of optimized intracryst. structure in improving the SIB electrode performance of layered titanate.  The creation of turbostratic in-plane structure degrades the SIB electrode performance of layered titanate, indicating the detrimental effect of in-plane structural disorder on electrode activity. 23Na magic-angle spinning NMR spectroscopy demonstrates that the n-alkylamine-intercalated titanates possess two different interlayer Na+ sites near ammonium head groups/titanate layers and near alkyl chains.  The intercalation of long-chain mols. increases the population of the latter site and the overall mobility of Na+ ions, which is responsible for the improvement of electrode activity upon n-alkylamine intercalation.  The present study highlights that the increased population of interlayer metal sites remote from the host layers is effective in improving the electrode functionality of layered metal oxide for SIBs and multivalent ion batteries.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref6"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref6" class="rightTabRefNumLink">6</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit6" data-doi="10.1107/S0567739476001551"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shannon, R.                 10.1016/j.nanoen.2015.05.012</span> </span><div class=" links-group getFTR"><div class="getFTR__content getFTR__placeholder"></div><div class="casRecord" id="
                        rightTab-cas_cit8R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">8</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Enhancing sodium-ion battery performance with interlayer-expanded MoS2-PEO nanocomposites</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Li, Yifei; Liang, Yanliang; Robles Hernandez, Francisco C.; Deog Yoo, Hyun; An, Qinyou; Yao, Yan</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Nano Energy</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:date">2015</span>),
    <span class="NLM_cas:volume">15</span>
        (<span class="NLM_cas:issue"></span>),

        ISSN:<span class="NLM_cas:issn">2211-2855</span>.
    
            (<span class="NLM_cas:orgname">Elsevier Ltd.</span>)
        </div><div class="casAbstract">The larger ionic radius of Na ion (1.06 Å) compared with that of Li ion (0.76 Å) is a fundamental reason for the inferior diffusion kinetics of Na ion in intercalation hosts.  Here we report interlayer expansion of intercalation hosts as a general strategy to facilitate the solid-state diffusion of Na ions.  Based on this strategy, poly(ethylene oxide)-intercalated MoS2 composites (PEO-MoS2) were synthesized via a facile exfoliation-restacking method and tested as anode materials for Na-ion batteries (NIBs).  The interlayer spacing of MoS2 was increased from 0.615 nm to 1.45 nm by insertion of controlled amts. of PEO. MoS2 (com-MoS2), and shows improved rate performance due to enhanced Na-ion diffusivity. It is well known that electrochem. insertion of Na+ into graphite is significantly hindered by the insufficient interlayer spacing.  Here we report expanded graphite as a Na-ion battery anode. KLT is prepd. by a low-temp. solid-state reaction and then transformed into NLT by replacing K with Na in a NaCl soln. at room temp. For NLT, extremely high discharging rate capability is achieved with a capacity of &gt;80 mA h g-1 at a 60 s full discharge and even with 70 mA h g-1 at a 34 s charge.  Kinetics anal. based on cyclic voltammogram reveals a typical Na-ion intercalation behavior in NLT.  Also, the 1st-principle calcn. shows a lower migration energy barrier for Na ions in NLT than that in other layered titanates. Nowadays, electrochem. energy storage technologies and applications have attracted much attention, including portable elec. devices, elec. vehicles and smart power grids.  Lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) have been widely applied in these areas because of their safety, portability and high energy d.  Nevertheless, the resources of lithium are limited and the vast consumption of lithium has pushed up the price of lithium compds., urging people to search for resourceful materials.                         rightTab-cas_cit24R"><div class="casContent"><span class="casTitleNuber">24</span><div class="casTitle"><span class="NLM_cas:atitle">Titanate Anodes for Sodium Ion Batteries</span></div><div class="casAuthors">Doeff, Marca M.; Cabana, Jordi; Shirpour, Mona</div><div class="citationInfo"><span class="NLM_cas:title">Journal of Inorganic and Organometallic Polymers and Materials</span>

        </div><div class="casAbstract">For reasons of cost and supply security issues, there is growing interest in the development of rechargeable sodium ion batteries, particularly for large-scale grid storage applications.  Like the much better known and technol. important lithium ion analogs, the devices operate by shuttling alkali metal cations between two host materials, which undergo insertion processes at different electrochem. potentials.  A particular challenge for the sodium systems is identification of a suitable anode material due to the fact that sodium does not intercalate into graphite.  Although several alternatives, including disordered carbons and alloys are being investigated, the most promising options at present lie with titanates, not in the least because of attractive characteristics such as low toxicity, ease of synthesis, wide availability, and low cost.  A large variety of sodium titanate compds. can be prepd., many of which have tunnel or layered structures that can readily undergo reversible reductive intercalation reactions.  A brief overview of the phys., structural, and electrochem. characteristics of several of the most promising materials for sodium-ion battery applications is given in this paper, and a comparison is made between the sodium and the lithium insertion behaviors.  For some of these compds., insertion of sodium occurs at unusually low potentials, a feature that has important implications for the design of high-energy sodium-ion systems.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref25"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref25" class="rightTabRefNumLink">25</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit25" data-doi="10.1039/C6EE01807F"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Guo, S.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Yi, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Sun, Y.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Zhou, H.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Recent Advances in Titanium-Based Electrode Materials for Stationary Sodium-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Energy Environ.         </div><div class="casAbstract">Recently, the attention to sodium-ion batteries has been refocused on large-scale energy storage applications, due to sodium's low cost and infinite abundance.  Sodium is one of the most abundant elements on earth and exhibits chem. properties similar to lithium.  Owing to their superior sodium storage capability esp. for excellent safety and stability, Ti-based compds. have been extensively investigated as both cathode and anode materials.  Herein we outline the current cathodes and anodes, and emphasize the crit. roles of titanium in developing advanced electrodes for sodium-ion batteries.  The latest advances and progress in the exploration of Ti-based compds. with various different frameworks such as NASICON, tunnel, MXenes, spinel, and layered structures are systematically reviewed.  The straightforward linking of the structure-function-property relationship for Ti-based compds., esp. for layered Na/Ti-contg. oxides, is summarized and analyzed.  The titanium element plays a crit. role in both pos. and neg. electrodes, i.e., supplying the charge transfer and high safety for anodes and greatly enhancing the structural and cycling stability for cathodes.  Based on the bi-functional roles of titanium, a new concept of sym. Na-ion cells employing layered Na/Ti-contg. oxides as bipolar electrodes is proposed and realized.  Sym. Na-ion cells already offered a high voltage and withstood long time charge-discharge processes, demonstrating the practicality beyond the proof of concept.  The participation of titanium in sodium-based electrode materials will greatly promote the development of room-temp. sodium-ion batteries towards stationary energy storage.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref26"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref26" class="rightTabRefNumLink">26</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit26" data-doi="10.1021/cm500342m"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Shirpour, M.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Cabana, J.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Doeff, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Lepidocrocite-type Layered Titanate Structures: New Lithium and Sodium Ion Intercalation Anode Materials</span>. <i>Chem.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The electrochem. characteristics of lepidocrocite-type titanates derived from K0.8Ti1.73Li0.27O4 are presented for the first time.  By exchanging sodium ions for potassium, the practical specific capacity of the titanate in both sodium and lithium half cells is considerably enhanced.  Although the gross structural features of the titanate framework are maintained during the ion exchange process, the symmetry changes because sodium occupies different sites from potassium.  The smaller size of the sodium ion as compared to potassium and the change in site symmetry allow more alkali metal cations to be inserted reversibly into the structure during discharge in sodium and lithium cells than in the parent compd.  Insertion of lithium cations takes place at an av. of about 0.8 V vs Li+/Li while sodium intercalation occurs at 0.5 V vs Na+/Na, with sloping voltage profiles exhibited for both cell configurations, implying single-phase processes.  Ex situ synchrotron X-ray diffraction measurements show that a lithiated lepidocrocite is formed during discharge in lithium cells, which undergoes further lithium insertion with almost no vol. change.  In sodium cells, insertion of sodium initially causes an overall expansion of about 12% in the b lattice parameter, but reversible uptake of solvent minimizes changes upon further cycling.  In the case of the sodium cells, both the practical capacity and the cyclability are improved when a more compliant binder (polyacrylic acid) that can accommodate vol. changes assocd. with insertion processes is used in place of the more common polyvinylidene fluoride.  The ability to tune the electrochem. properties of lepidocrocite titanate structures by varying compns. and utilizing ion exchange processes make them esp. versatile anode materials for both lithium and sodium ion battery configurations.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref27"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref27" class="rightTabRefNumLink">27</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit27" data-doi="10.1021/acsaem.8b00170"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Reeves, K.         </div><div class="casAbstract">A lamellar lepidocrocite-type titanate structure with ∼25% Ti4+ vacancies was recently synthesized, and it showed potential for use as an electrode in rechargeable lithium-ion batteries.  In addn. to Li, we explore this material's ability to accommodate other monovalent ions with greater natural abundance (e.g., Na and K) in order to develop lower-cost alternatives to Li-ion batteries constructed from more widely available elements.  Galvanostatic discharge/charge curves for the lepidocrocite material indicate that increasing the ionic radius of the monovalent ion results in a deteriorating performance of the electrode.  Using 1st-principles electronic structure calcns., we identify the relaxed geometries of the structure for various placement of the ion in the structure.  We then use these geometries to compute the energy of formations.  We det. that all ions are favorable in the structure, but interlayer positions are preferred compared to vacancy positions.  We also conclude that the exchange between the interlayer and vacancy positions is a process which involves the interaction between interlayer water and surface hydroxyl groups next to the titanate layer.  We observe a cooperative effect between structural water and OH groups to assist alkali-ions to move from the interlayer to the vacancy site.  The as-synthesized lepidocrocite serves as a prototypical structure to study both the migration mechanism of ions within a confined space along with the interaction between water mols. and the titanate framework.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref28"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref28" class="rightTabRefNumLink">28</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit28" data-doi="10.1021/acs.chemmater.6b03928"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Vasileiadis, A.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Wagemaker, M.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Thermodynamics and Kinetics of Na-Ion Insertion into Hollandite-TiO<sub>2</sub> and O3-Layered NaTiO<sub>2</sub>: An Unexpected Link between Two Promising Anode Materials for Na-Ion Batteries</span>. <i>Chem. The thin film prepn. of the layered materials in layer-by-layer fashion can be realized by several soln. processes.  However, the layered materials suffer low thermal stability after the soln. processes.  Herein, we report a strategy to improve the thermal stability of the layered materials processed in soln.  In this work, we studied the thermal stability of the lepidocrocite-type titanate with various interlayer ions (Li+, Na+, K+, and Cs+) at elevated temps.  We proved that the thermal stability of the titanate increased with the increase of the ionic radius.  The Cs+ intercalated titanate can remain in its layered structure up to 1000°C, while the Li+ interacted titanate loses its structural stability at ∼280°C.  Our work suggests that increasing the size of the interlayer ions is an effective strategy to enhance the structural stability of layered titanates.</div></div></div></div></div></div></li><li id="rightTab-ref33"><div class="reference"><strong class="refLabel"><a href="#ref33" class="rightTabRefNumLink">33</a></strong><div class="NLM_citation references__item" id="rightTab-cit33" data-doi="10.1103/PhysRevB.54.11169"><span><span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Kresse, G.</span></span>; <span class="NLM_contrib-group"><span class="NLM_string-name">Furthmüller, J.</span></span> <span> </span><span class="NLM_article-title">Efficient Iterative Schemes for Ab Initio Total-Energy Calculations Using a Plane-Wave Basis Set</span>. <i>Phys. In the first part the application of Pulay's DIIS method (direct inversion in the iterative subspace) to the iterative diagonalization of large matrixes will be discussed.  This approach is stable, reliable, and minimizes the no. of order Natoms3 operations.  In the second part, we will discuss an efficient mixing scheme also based on Pulay's scheme.  A special "metric" and a special "preconditioning" optimized for a plane-wave basis set will be introduced. This procedure is justified when the error in ExcDFA arises from the λ = 0 or exchange end of the coupling-const. integral ∫01dλ Exc,λDFA.         </div><div class="casAbstract">The method of dispersion correction as an add-on to std. Kohn-Sham d. functional theory (DFT-D) has been refined regarding higher accuracy, broader range of applicability, and less empiricism.  The main new ingredients are atom-pairwise specific dispersion coeffs. and cutoff radii that are both computed from first principles.  The coeffs. for new eighth-order dispersion terms are computed using established recursion relations.  System (geometry) dependent information is used for the first time in a DFT-D type approach by employing the new concept of fractional coordination nos. (CN).  They are used to interpolate between dispersion coeffs. of atoms in different chem. environments.  The method only requires adjustment of two global parameters for each d. functional, is asymptotically exact for a gas of weakly interacting neutral atoms, and easily allows the computation of at. forces.  Three-body nonadditivity terms are considered.  The method has been assessed on std. benchmark sets for inter- and intramol. noncovalent interactions with a particular emphasis on a consistent description of light and heavy element systems.  The mean abs. deviations for the S22 benchmark set of noncovalent interactions for 11 std. d. functionals decrease by 15%-40% compared to the previous (already accurate) DFT-D version.  Spectacular improvements are found for a tripeptide-folding model and all tested metallic systems.  The rectification of the long-range behavior and the use of more accurate C6 coeffs. also lead to a much better description of large (infinite) systems as shown for graphene sheets and the adsorption of benzene on an Ag(111) surface.  For graphene it is found that the inclusion of three-body terms substantially (by about 10%) weakens the interlayer binding.  We propose the revised DFT-D method as a general tool for the computation of the dispersion energy in mols. and solids of any kind with DFT and related (low-cost) electronic structure methods for large systems. Av. and local structures of Na2Ti9O19 are elucidated from neutron Rietveld refinement and pair distribution function (PDF), resp., to investigate the initial discharge and charge events.
